A WEEK'S PEACE JUBILEE.
Entertainment at Grace Methodist
Church on Twenty-First Street.
The parlors of Grace Methodist Church
on Capp and Twenty-first streets will be
occupied during the present week by the
ladies of the congregation and their num
erous friends for the holding of a peace
jubilee. In order to make the entertain
ment as attractive as possible hot dinners
will be served each evening between the
hours of 5:30 and 7:30. for the moderate
price of 25 cents. After dinner the pro
gramme will be varied with social at
tractions. A great assortment of novel
articles, holiday presents, winter supplies
and many other useful as well as orna
mental selections will be offered for sale.
The entertainment last evening was for
the benefit of the Church Extension So
ciety, w-hich held its twelfth annual tea
reception and reunion.
The use of the church parlors was
cheerfully accorded by the jubilee com
mitee to the society for this occasion.
The popularity of both entertainments
had the effect of filling every nook and
corner of the edifice.
The object of this extension society is:
To seek out new places for missionary
work in this city; to establish Sunday
schools and preaching places; also to re
lieve overburdened churches, and to assist
missionaries who may be appointed by
the authority of the California Annual
Conference of the Methodist Episcopal
Church.
The trustees of the society are: Charles
Goodall, William Abbott, C. S. Holmes,
W P. Higginbotham, I. J. Truman C. 13.
Perkins, R. V. Watt, J. W. Whiting.
Andrew Nelson, Robert McElroy.
J. W. Wetmore. Permanent offi
cers, who are annually elected:
Honorary president, Hon. Charles Good
all; Honorary vice presidents. Bishop J.
P. Newman, LL. D.. W. W. Case, D. D.,
Hon. Annis Merrill, C. S. Holmes; presi
dent, I. J. Truman; vice presidents, Wil
liam Abbott, J. W. Whiting, R. V. Watt,
C. B. Perkins; treasurer. Columbian
Banking Co.; financial secretary, C. A.
Maydwell; secretary, William M. Abbott.
MINERS MEET TO
ELECT OFFICERS
DELEGATES TO THE STATE CON
VENTION ALSO CHOSEN.
Julian Sonntag Elected President of
the ban Francisco County
Association.
Julian Sonntag was elected president of
the San Francisco County Miners' Asso
ciation at the annual meeting held at the
Chamber of Commerce yesterday after
noon. T. J. Parson was placed in nomin
ation for another term, Mr. Sonntag ex
pressing the sentiment that a change was
not desirable, as Mr. Parsons had admin
istered the affairs of the office in an ac-
ceptable manner.
On account of failing health and busi
ness exactions Mr. Parsons was con
strained to decline the honor of further
service as president. Thereupon Charles
G. Tale suggested Mr. Sonntag for the
presidency and the latter was elected by
acclamation. In accepting the duties of
the position the new president expressed
pleasure in seeing so many members at
the meeting. He predicted a great State
Convention of Miners at Native Sons'
Hall next week. Speaking of a recent
visit to Nevada City he said he was as
sured that Nevada County would send
eighty delegates. Information had been
received that Amador County would send
forty delegates; El Dorado, thirty; Butte,
eight; Santa Clara, 5, and that there
would be full representation by Placer
County.
In accordance with custom the chair
named a committee of five to recommend
vice-president, secretary-treasurer and
delegates to the State convention. The
committee, consisting of Lou!s Glass. W.
C. Ralston, Daniel Wilson, Nlles Searls
and J. F. Halloran withdrew for confer
ence and the convention took a recess.
The committee in due time reported,
recommending for vice president. J. F.
Halloran, and for secretary and treasurer,
Charles G. Yale. The convention elected
the officers so recommended.
The following delegates to the State
convention were recommended and
chosen:
W. W. Montague, Nlles Searls, J. F. Hal
loran Louis Glass, E. A. Rlx, P. J. Hendy, B.
T. Lacy, A. T. Scott, George E. Dow, W. G.
Dodd. A. J. KaJston, P. Mooney. H. J. Lally.
W. C. Ralston, John Martin. A. S. Cooper, T.
J. Parsons, Edward Coleman, Dr. E. Lichean.
R. R. Grayson, D. E. Hayes, John C. Coleman,
C. W. Cross, Georjre Stone, Henry R. Taylor.
P. George Gow, Hugh Craig. John Berming
ham, E. A. Belcher, Julius Sonnta*, Charles G.
Yale, George C. Sargent, A. Carrigan and T.
J. Barbour.
President Sonntag gave notice that he
would announce the new directors to-day.
The convention then adjourned.

Mamie Sryce and Katie Cliffe, two
young women, were the guests of George
Barnabee, S64VÂ£ Howard street, Sunday
night, and after partaking liberally of his
hospitality they left, as Barnabee had to
go to his work. They returned to the
house and stole the carpet and other ar
ticles, leaving only the bedstead and bu
reau in the room. Yesterday Barnabee
told his woes to Policeman W. J. Smith,
and he arrested the two young women on
a charge of petty larceny.

He Made Cigars Midst Unutterable Filth
and Inspectors Dockery and Davis
Closed His Shop.
Mr. Lee On, of 1114 Dupont street, a
maker of cigars of questionable ante
cedents and dubious quality, has, per
force, sur-pended, business and the Health
Department has padlocked his doors
against him until such time as he may
prevail upon his landlord to put his filthy
hovel in a fairly sanitary condition.
Lee On's factory has been under the eye
of the Health Department ever since the
crusade was begun against the reeking
dens in Chinatown. Cigar Inspector B.
R. Porter reported that the place should
be condemned six months ago, and from
time to time since the wily On has been
warned to shut up or clean up, with the
result that he has done neither the one
nor the other in good Celestial fashion.
On Monday Inspector Dockery gave him
notice to quit by next day â and he didn't.

MALICE SPED
THE BULLET
SAYS BERG
The Second Shot Was
Fired at Mrs. Elk.
INJURED MAN MAY RECOVER
NO LIGHT AS YET THROWN ON
THE BROOKS MURDER.
Mrs. Elk Visits Her Husband and
Then Calls Upon His Victim.
District Attorney Marti
nelli Criticized.
Nick Berg, the wounded boatkeeper,
who was shot by Ike Elk, now has a
fighting chance to recover, according to
Dr. Arthur H. Mays. Ever since he was
wounded Berg has been cheerful, and did
not think he would die. Yesterday after
noon he consented to talk to a reporter.
"I want to contradict some of the things
I am reported to have said," he declared.
"In the first place I have hitherto said
not a single word to any newspaperman
and Dr. Mays has refused to let any of.
them in to see me.
"I started for the Chispa from Captain
Roberts' yacht at Tiburon about 7 o'clock.
I met a fisherman near the Chispa and
I he told me that Klk and his wife were
both on board the yacht. When I went on
board I knocked on the cabin door and
c:illed 'Ike! Ike! Let me in.' The only
response I got was a grunt and then I
went to the hatchway and removed it.
This talk of my breaking the hatchway
is all nonsense. It wag loose and I sim
ply lifted it off. As the cover came off a
shot rant? out and 1 felt a pain in my
breast. Then there was another shot,
and pretty soon Klk and his wife came
out. He was fully dressed but she was in
her night clothing.
"I asked Elk what he shot me for and
ho made no answer. Then Mrs. Elk made
him take a boat and row me to shore. AYe
left him and walked up to tind Dr. Crump
ton. On the way she told me that Ike
recognized my voice and would not let
her open the door or even answer.
"As regards the Brooks murder I know
nothing of it, and, so far as my knowl
edge extends, I don't think Ike does. He
shot me out of pure jealousy and for no
other reason. I was on the yacht with
him and his wife last Thursday and he :
was in a good humor them.
'About two weeks ago he tried to kill
me out of Jealousy, and 1 stopped him.
Mrs. Elk teils me that the second shot >
Elk fired was at her and not at me. When
he reached town that night he remarked
to some acquaintances that he had in- :
tended to shoot me for a long time and
had finally succeeded."
"How do you account for the fact that j
three chambers of the revolver you were !
3hot with had been discharged previous
ly?" he was asked.
â 'Well. I don't remember how many !
were, discharged, but 1 had been in the 1
habit of taking shots at sralions now and '
then. Elk shot me with full intent. He
knew who I was. The Brooks murder had
nothing to do with it at all."
At this juncture Berg grew weak from
his exertion and his attendant would not i
permit him to say anything more.
The indifference of District Attorney
Martinelli of Marin County in this case
is the subject of severe criticism by the
citizens of that county. Martinelli de
clared yesterday that he had not taken
any statement from Berg or Elk and fur
thermore he did not intend to make any
attempt to elicit any information on this
case or the Brooks murder from either ol
them. He said he was satisfied neither
would talk, so he made no move. His
apathy is attributed to the fact that he
goes out of office on January 1.

WRIGHT WILL
BE SPEAKER OF
THE ASSEMBLY
His Candidacy Is Well
Received.
FAVORED BY ALL CLASSES
IS PROMISED A PRACTICALLY
UNANIMOUS VOTE.
Friends of L. H. Valentine of Los
Angeles Do Not Believe His
Name Will Be Pre
sented/
Aside from the Senatorial contest the
organization of the Legislature and the
selection of the man who will serve as
Speaker of the Assembly remains the
one topic of interest among politicians
and those actively interested in the
events of the next four or five months.
As to the Speakership, the tide seems
I to be setting strongly in the direction
I of Assemblyman Howard E. Wright of
I Berkeley, whose candidacy was an
! nounced almost two weeks ago. It is
| everywhere recognized and acknowl
\ edged that the coming session of the
! Legislature will be one of the most im
| portant ever held in this State, and
I for this reason, if no other, it is con
ceded that the presiding officer of the
Assembly should be a man who will
I command the confidence and respect
] not only of the members of the Assem-
I bly, but of the people of the entire
| State.
That Mr. Wright is such a man. it
is unnecessary to assert, as his record
as a legislator is above reproach and
his ability to perform in a satisfactory
manner the multitudinous duties of the
position is well known to all. Since
the announcement of his candidacy he
has been the recipient of many assur
ances of support from Assemblymen
elect in all sections of the State, as well
as from prominent men of affairs in
and out of politics. These assurances
are of such a nature and are so numer
ous that there is little doubt that Mr.
Wright will receive practically the
unanimous vote of the Assembly.
The only other candidate for the
Speakership who can, at this time, be
looked upon as strong enough to con
sider his own claims with seriousness
is L. H. Valentine of Los Angeles. Val
entine has announced his candidacy,
but reports received from Los Angeles
and vicinity within the past twenty
four hours indicate that his most inti
mate political friends do not hope to se
cure for him sufficient recognition to

The Democratic members of the lower
house of the Legislature are taking an
active interest in the contest for the
Speakership, for the reason that un
less a fair minded and thoroughly up
right Speaker is selected by the major
ity the minority will receive little or
no consideration in the matter of pro
posed or pending legislation, or in de
bate. The Democratic vote will be
given to a Democratic member, possN
bly A. Caminetti; but it will be purely
complimentary, there being no possibil
ity of the election of a Democrat to
preside over a body the majority of
the members of which are of the oppo
site political faith.
The public is hereby informed that Eu
gene Rosenthal and nurse have not been
connected with the Red Cross of Califor
nia later than September 22. Mrs. W. B.
Harrington, President California Red
Cross State Association.
Suit Ag-ainst the Tiburon.
Assistant United States District Attor
ney Schlesinger filed suit yesterday in the
United States District Court against the
steamer Tiburon to collect a penalty of
$200 for failing to signal the United States
revenue cutter Rush while passing 1 that
vessel on the bay.
